  - If Track B shows positive coalition signals without disturbing the main baseline, push a measured step (e.g., a small, public adjustment that doesn’t threaten Pencil or top items).
  - If Track B stalls, revert to Track A’s public tweak or pause track testing to reassess strategy with all five players.
5) Proposed Round 3–Round 4 path (short plan)
- Public Round 3 framing (as agreed): main baseline locked; Track B moves Jewel 4 → 3 in parallel; Track A 4 → 2 as a reversible fallback.
- Round 3 vote outcome: expect affirmation of the main baseline (A) and Track B (B) as the primary parallel path, with Track A as fallback if needed (C optional depending on vote results).

- I want Jewel to remain accessible as a lever but never at the cost of Pencil’s protection or the integrity of the main baseline.

- Pencil remains the dominant sticking point. Proposals that keep Pencil in the main baseline (Agent_5) continue to win buy-in; any move of Pencil in the main track is a deal-breaker for me.
- Jewel as a lever works best when tested in parallel (Track B). Track B tends to generate more acceptances than moving Jewel in the main baseline, but consensus is still hard because Jewel’s location interacts with other top items.
- The main baseline (Quill-1, Apple-2, Stone-3, Jewel-4, Pencil-5) is the strongest common ground. Proposals that preserve that baseline tend to get more support, even if that means accepting smaller or more incremental changes in the parallel space.
Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible
  - Agent_1 (Quill) and Agent_2 (Apple) clearly prefer keeping their top items in the main baseline.
  - Agent_5 (Pencil) requires Pencil to stay in the main baseline; this is a shared anchor for consensus.
  - Agent_4 (Jewel) is flexible about Jewel being tested in parallel (Track B) and is comfortable with a main baseline staying intact.
- Conflicting
  - Agent_3 (Stone) and Agent_4 (Jewel) diverge on Jewel’s location. Agent_3 prefers leveraging Jewel in Track B (parallel) for a tangible uplift, while Agent_4 wants to keep Jewel accessible (ideally in the main baseline, unless a clean parallel swap can be made).
  - The tension centers on whether Jewel should stay in the main baseline or be moved in parallel in a way that still keeps Pencil protected.
What blocks consensus
- Pencil’s main-baseline location is non-negotiable for me; any plan that shifts Pencil in the main baseline stalls consensus.
- Jewel’s location remains sensitive: moving to Agent_3 in parallel helps some, but not all, coalitions; moving Jewel into the main baseline faces opposition unless balanced with concessions that don’t harm Pencil.

- Main baseline (unchanged core): Quill-1, Apple-2, Stone-3, Jewel-4, Pencil-5.
- Track B (primary parallel test, public): Jewel moves 4 → 3 in parallel; Pencil stays 5 in main baseline; Quill/Apple/Stone stay in main baseline.

- Consider small, reversible adjustments in Track B that do not touch Pencil, such as modestly reallocating Stone or Jewel within the parallel space (still keeping Pencil fixed in the main baseline).

- Step 1: Validate Track B as the default Round 4 parallel test with a crisp public framing.
- Step 2: If Track B yields any coalition signals, extend Track B incrementally in Round 4 (e.g., move Jewel 3 → 2 in parallel), again with Pencil fixed in main baseline.
- Step 3: If Track B stalls, rely on Track A as the fallback, but only with explicit guardrails and no Pencil movements in the main baseline.
- Step 4: Use a “coalition map” to show who benefits from Track B changes and keep Pencil outcomes tied to the main baseline so others can see where gains lie.

- Option A (Track B as default)
  - Public framing: Main baseline locked. Track B tests Jewel 4 → 3 in parallel; Pencil fixed at 5. Track A available as a reversible fallback (Jewel 4 → 2). Round 4 will assess Track B traction and decide whether to extend or revert.
- Option B (Track A as fallback)
  - Public framing: Main baseline locked. Track B tests Jewel 4 → 3 in parallel; Track A tests Jewel 4 → 2 in parallel as a safety valve if Track B stalls. Pencil stays at 5 in the main baseline. Round 4 reassesses.

  - Confirm Track B as the Round 4 primary parallel test with explicit guardrails (Pencil fixed, moves reversible).
  - If Track B gains traction, escalate in small steps (e.g., 4 → 3 in Round 4, then 3 → 2 in Round 5 if warranted).
